RATING: 7.5
I think this is a game with a steep learning curve. Much of the strategy comes form the initial drafting phase, which is a very dry, calculating exercise. This means beginners have to pick things up fast to compete, or they will be left behind for the whole game. Future games should run smoother. It's certainly clever in the card interactions and a good drafting/set collection game. The artwork is beautiful but overly busy and limits functionality. The board is disappointingly small, but the chunky dice with nice clear iconography are great. A mixed bag, and I walked away from the game a little non-plussed, but it has been on my mind a lot since, and now I really want to play it again. Mechanically with all that drafting, it has obvious connections with 7 Wonders, but to me it felt a lot like At The Gates of Loyang too, with the tableau of cards building up in front of you, conversion of one resource into another, the changing market, and limited interaction. I love Loyang, but find the "magic crystals" theme far less enticing. Yes, I definitely want to play this again.

RATING: 5
I liked the drafting and the very interesting use of different kinds of dice. The system how you acquire resources and play the cards is quite fun as well.

Definitely not a 4-player game. The first couple of rounds are quite fast but once players have laid a few cards on the table and start using their powers, each turn will start to drag. With increasing player numbers the game also has more potential to spiral down into whirlpool of unfun. It is almost certain that the few cards absorbing and destroying victory points from other players will get played. After this the players not owning those cards have no incentive to make any VPs in the mid game since they will be lost anyway. Henceforth players will only wait for the very last round of the game and score the points they can. Of course this is a valid strategy but I find it rather dull if you have no meaningful decision to make for a major part of the game. 

Another bad design choice is that the card drafting is done completely at the very beginning. That means that you have basically locked down your whole game with very little room for reactive maneuvers. Of course you can draw more cards but usually you just try to play the initial ones as well to avoid the VP penalty from held cards at the end. I really would have liked a possibility to change direction and actually react to what other players are doing.

The rest of my criticism is directed at rather minor things such as the art and use of symbols. I love the art but for some reason it feel really out of place in this game. The game, the theme and the art just do not fit together although all three are good alone. For symbols, the VPs and the flames look a little bit too alike. But these are really minor complaints.

In a nutshell, the funniest part of the game takes place during the initial drafting. Creating combos and figuring out in which order to play the cards can be quite fun. But in order to minimise the duration of the more scripted part, I would really recommend playing with 2 or at maximum 3 players.

RATING: 5.5
Seasons is a fine game, but it just leaves me feeling "meh" and it's hard to put my finger on why.  Part of the reason is probably that the theme is not very interesting to me, and the theme doesn't feel deeply integrated into the game.  On top of that, the decisions in the game aren't that interesting.  You rarely have more than three cards in hand, and the results on the dice usually aren't that different.  The game utilizes a variety of different mechanics, but doesn't really do anything interesting or unique with them.  If I wanted to do card drafting, I'd play 7 Wonders.  If I wanted to play with dice, I'd play Castles of Burgundy.  If I wanted to do resource management, I'd play Village, or Agricola, or Caylus, or any number of games that do it better.  Heck, if I wanted a game with cards, dice, and resources, I'd rather play Stone Age.

A lot of people really like this game, but I have a hard time seeing why.  It's not a bad game, but for me at least, it's just kind of dull.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
+ Orb of Ragfield, Crystal Titan and Speedwall the Escaped.

Such a clever and fun game! There're so many reasons for me to love Seasons. The graphics and the components are certainly something that draws you in: those dice look and feel awesome! I enjoy the mechanic of the the calendar, which introduces a strong time management aspect to Magic-style card games like this, as well as thr "dice drafting". Yet what I really like about the game is its "draft and play" nature. I loved drafting when I used to play Magic: The Gathering, but it was expensive. In this box I have the opportunity to draft as much as I want and explore so many cool combos and combinations.

Sure there's a relevant luck element. I don't mean the dice, because the luck there is easily balanced over time, but the cards. It's REALLY important to draw new cards during the game and, if you get lucky, you can really obtain a huge advantage over the others at the table. Still this is a game I'm very glad to have in my collection and one I'll gladly play every now and then. 

Rating without the expansions: 7.5
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This game nicely combines dice rolling with deck building. The game revolves around a central board split into four parts, the four seasons. Each season has a special set of dice, which you roll and execute the rolled action: collect resources, collect bonus point and buy cards. The cards bought have victory point and also special  effects which you can activate by spending the apropiate resources. The game is fun and quick paced, the design is wonderful. Although the cards are not the diversified, there any many copies.

RATING: 5
A fairly simple game of dice rolling for resources to summon cards out for VPs.

As the cards are initially drafted, the VPs is already half done and decided. The other half is how the game unfolds with the different die rolls to maximize the profit.

Random chaos that is both fun (to roll) and boring (activate) at the same time. Lots of reading to do for first 1-2 plays.

Easy gateway game for beginners to boardgames. Veterans will find this light. Even if they like it, it's for a certain group of gamers.

Very average rating.

RATING: 4
The first time I played [i]Seasons[/i] was back in September 2013. The rating then was a three.

Fast forward to November 15, 2015. I had forgotten I had played the game. The person teaching opens the game box, and I recognize it. 

I learn the game again. She does a fairly good job of explaining the game, decides to skip a part of it that only benefits experienced players, and the experience is better.

Not great, but better.

My rating went up to four, and while I still don't like the game, I may have been a smidgen too forceful with the original review. The real problem isn't the number of cards, but how you need to draft a deck on the fly at the very beginning of the game, with no guarantee that you'll get the tokens you need to execute your plan.

Essentially, your first few moves are playing blind.

So, as I said once, "I can see why some people would like it, although I've never understood why people find those games enjoyable."

[i]Original Review:[/i]
The game is far too random, and there are too many cards to keep track of. I can see why some people would like it, although I've never understood why people find those games enjoyable.

RATING: 8

RATING: 7
A unique dice-drafting mechanic gives each player a different combination of actions in every round, which they can use to gather energy, crystals, and artifact cards to become the top wizard in all the land.  Easy to learn and easy to teach.

Seasons is a good game, but with a better set of cards, it could be a great game. Each card provides the controller with some sort of special ability, and there are combinations of cards that nearly eliminate the need for energy (resources), or combinations that severely restrict other players' abilities to play cards or abilities, which severely restricts their ability to actually enjoy the game. There is also an issue where some cards pay off over time, while others have abilities that don't matter when you get them.  These problems would be fairly minor if the only cards you received were the ones that you chose in the draft at the beginning of the game, but there is also the possibility of gaining cards throughout the game, making it fairly common for one player to get hindered by drawing cards in the wrong order, or for a player to assemble a ridiculous combo without anyone being able to do anything about it.  It doesn't always happen, but when it does the game can be miserable.

The components in this game are amazing.  The art is good, though I'm not a fan of the anime-like aesthetic, the dice are chunky, the cardboard counters are thick, and the box insert has a place for everything, even after the cards are sleeved, 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
What a fantastic game. The art is beautiful, the cards are synergistic, the theme works really well (it is cool to imagine the game actually taking place over three years, with powerful wizards tapping the world around them for week son end to procure energy, only to have a short winter so that the wind energy becomes hard to find!), and the game plays quickly once you know the rules and have become somewhat familiar with the cards. Expansions work really well, too.

If you are into strategy games and have a history with MTG, this is the game for you. If you don't want to sit down and learn what all the cards do and how the strategy works, STILL PLAY THIS GAME. If you despise reading cards and can't stand thinking multiple turns in advance, then maybe pass this game up, but everyone else should give it a fair shake.

RATING: 6
Really wanted to love this one - the mechanisms (dice drafting, card drafting, hand management, deckbuilding, etc.) seem built for my personal preferences - and maybe if I were to play with the expansions everything would click, but for me, this game is just too fiddly (that score-tracker is just awful!) and limited.

Yes, there are 50 cards in the set [2 copies each make 100, which is another problem - 2 copies of each card in a 2 player game mean that you frequently have the same cards as your opponent], but only a limited set of those are used in a given game, which means (usually) there are no surprises, especially since you draft to assemble your starting hand. By the time you've played two or three times, you've basically seen what the cards have to offer, and it's not that wide-ranging.

The card portion feels like a half-hearted attempt at Magic or an LCG/CCG, but it falls far short because of the limited selection. The drafting portion doesn't compete well with a whole-hearted card-drafter like 7 Wonders, and just leaves you wishing they had executed better.

Disappointing, on the whole. Maybe the expansions improve the game (certainly they add in missing pieces - see the holes in the player aids), but the core game on its own was not good enough merit another round of financial investment.

RATING: 6
Nem lenne ez rossz játék, csak van benne pár bosszantó hiba... Ami tetszik, az a draftolás az elején. Az alap taktika már ekkor eldől, hiszen előre meghatározzuk a későbbi lapjaink ütemezését. A sok kártya elég nagy varianciát biztosít, a nehezebb fokozatot nem is próbáltuk még. Az évszakváltások is jók, a játék hosszára hatással vagyunk a kockaválasztásnál. Az első bő fél órában nagyon tetszett: szép, ötletes, igényes játék. A bajok ott kezdődtek, amikor kezdett nyúlni, mint a rétes. Végül szabállyal együtt majdnem 3 órás volt (4 fős, igaz hármunknak az első parti volt), óriási holtidővel. A másik ami fura volt, hogy pillanatok alatt le tudtam tenni minden lapomat, új laphoz viszont csak szerencse révén juthatok, ha jut megfelelő kocka, így a játék felében nem nagyon tudtam mást csinálni, csak eladogatni az energiákat. A draftolás igazságos szerintem, de a később kihúzott lapok lutrivá teszik az egészet, simán fel lehet húzni 30 ingyen leépíthető pontot, ami a 100-200 körüli eredményekhez képest sok! A slusszpoén pedig, hogy az egyetlen olyan játékos nyert, aki végig csak kombózgatott magában, nem igazán törődve azzal, mit játszanak ki a többiek (akár ellene is), amivel nincs gond, de ha ez az általános, akkor megkérdőjeleződik a konfrontatív lapok értelme. És még egy dolog: a nagy matatásban, rengeteg kártya pakolgatásában simán elmozdulhatnak a jelölők, és utólag lehetetlen rekonstruálni, hogy mi hol állt...
Nem rossz ez a játék, de ha fele ilyen hosszú lenne, sokkal jobban élveztem volna.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Seasons is a gorgeous piece of work. It has awesome french-style artwork, big chunky dice and a top-notch production (it has one of the most functional box inserts I ever saw!).

The game itself is very well designed: it has big power cards that trump rules, a drafting system to put these cards in the hands of the players, a clever speed-defining system built-in in the dice, and many other small details that reveal a long time spent play testing and polishing the game.

It has some cons: there's not much a player can do during his opponents' turns, so the downtime could be a problem when playing with four AP-prone players; and sometimes it can feel more tactical than strategic.

Anyway, the game is very good, and initial rating (7.5) could rise if it can stand repeated plays!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Much of the fun of a TCG, but with a set card pool, dice rolls which heavily influence the tactics played and resource generation unlike many other games.

While it has dice, it uses them in the *ahem* correct way - you roll them at the start of each round, and everyone bases their choices on what turns up, not the other way round!

Really fun, quick and - if you can deal with the odd scoreboard - a satisfying game to play.

NB The draft at the start of the game determines a lot of the strategy, so it is advised to stick to some set hands at the start when introducing it to newbies.

RATING: 9
This game has shelved all of Race for the Galaxy, Glory to Rome and Magic the Gathering. It's just that good.

I like drafting cards and dice. The fact that the game can flow faster of slower throught the years is a nice detail, too.
The artwork is fantastic, and the components are of great quality.

I haven't played the begginner game (pre-built decks), but the intermediate game (cards 1-30) is a fantastic game on its own, so the fact there are another 40 cards for the full game is icing on the cake.
In fact, the intermediate game is so good, I'm still up for playing it anytime, even after playing the full game. It makes for a simpler, more predictable game, so you can go into the game with some strategy in mind.

RATING: 7.75
This was sold to me as M:TG drafting turned into a game, and it did not disappoint. The drafting mechanic is important, but it's only one way to build a strategy. You need to balance card draw with card play, and there are no 'useless' cards. The dice in particular are really clever - they create a shifting economy that really drives the rhythms of the game... not unlike the Seasons they are intended to represent.

It's a little heavier than most people can get into, sadly, which means it doesn't hit the table often, and not frequently enough with the same group that I've ever seenthe in-box expansion cards.

I'd like to play it more, and would like to play it enough to need to buy the expansins!

RATING: 7.5
This game feels like it could be played quicker than it does. It should be playable in an hour with three players, but somehow that has never happened. That's probably the biggest drawback for me though, because there's so much to like. Drafting cards for determining your strategy, making the best of what the dice throw your way, timing your card effects...

Depending on the cards that get drawn, there can be a reasonable amount of 'take that' in the game. But since you're drafting, there is a chance to mitigate. Not everyone likes this in their games though.

Also, the game looks great. It's the typical French comic book style in bright colors that appeals to me. There's heavy dice with custom symbols in different colors for each season and great artwork on the cards.

A tiny nagging issue is the small cubes on your player board. They shift the moment you merely scrape the board with your sleeve. It would have been so much better when there had been gaps or recesses for holding the track counters better.

Played three times with 2, 4, and 3 players, drafting cards each game, and, despite winning the third game, each play saw my opinion of the game decline.  The randomness of the cards and of the dice and the way the game can get bogged down both hurt the game for me.  The third year is painfully long it seems like.  The other issue is how fiddley the game can be.  This includes the scoreboard, which is pretty poor, but more significantly, it includes a lot of the cards.  A card that takes a point from one player and gives it to another, that earns crystals when you play another card, or that gives you something when the season changes are all way too fiddley.  I just got sick of it.  I had the card where everyone had to give me a point each time the season changed.  I started to feel really annoying after a few season changes.  Plus, if you forget to do something, which happens a ton, you just can't go back and do it, or can you?  What if someone wants to and someone else doesn't?  The game could be so much cleaner.  I'd likely be willing to play the game if someone else really wanted to, but I wouldn't expect to enjoy it.  

All this being said, I would probably buy an iOS app of the game if it came out.  The app would get rid of much of what was frustrating to me.

RATING: 7.5
Promos:
- Seasons: Air Elemental
- Seasons: Crystal Titan
- Seasons: Orb of Ragfield

This is a game I bought primarily because of the hype and fancy dice. 

Like Keyflower I finally got around to playing this game on 2/19/2013 because I need to run it at a convention over the weekend.

My first thoughts after playing this game was, "Well I can't see what all the hype is about.". I game fell alittle flat for me and my group but then I started to really think about it... We didn't really play by the rules. I don't meen that we cheated. We just made some changes to make the game easier to explain. Rather then explaining the cards in depth before the first play I just delt out 9 cards to each player. Each player then made 3 stacks of 3 cards at random. One was their starting hand, one was their year 2 cards and the other was their year 3 cards. We completly ignored the draft and upon later revewing of the rules the pregenerated hands. I have a feeling this took alot of the early strategy out of the game for us.

Looking back I definatly want to take a few more wacks at this game before making a final descision. 

Update - 2/26/2013

Taught this at a local game convention over the weekend. My impression on the second play through is "Man this game can really drag on." 

I'd still like to play it once more before I make my final descision.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
An interesting game of forming card c-c-c-c-c-combos in order to produce the most points possible!

The overall rules are very simple.  You'll draft some cards at the start of the game, getting some of them in each of the three phases of the game.

Then, in a round of play, some dice are rolled, and in turn order each player gets to pick one of the dice, which awards the player various stuff.  The most common stuff are elements, which you'll have to spend to put cards into play from your hand.  On your turn, you'll pick a die, and then play and activate as many cards as you'd like.

Cards do all sorts of stuff.  They can score you points, steal points from other players, get you more elements, allow you to draw more cards, etc.  The key is drafting and playing the cards in such a way as to maximize your score.  They're also key in giving you flexibility with which dice are good for you, as you definitely can't get on always getting exactly what you need from the dice.

Overall, just a unique combination of card and dice drafting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Picked this up just based on ratings I've seen. Initially we played it with 4 players, and we found it really confusing. All the game mechanics are interlinked and one can't easily be explained without knowing how the others work. Terminology takes a bit of getting used to. With "Power Crystals" read "Points". After a couple of playthroughs (with 2 players) it all became clear.

This is quite an American style game in that one person can be in the lead from the start and the others don't really have any chance to overtake, which can be quite frustrating the losing player. There can also be quite a lot of luck involved. However I think this is the kind of game a person could get really good at by learning tactics and knowing good combos of cards.

A lot of the cards have on-going effects and the player needs a sharp focus to remember all the things the cards do on his or her turn.

Lovely themed game and nice artwork. Probably better with 3 or 4 players. Shame there is no option for 5 or 6 players.

RATING: 9.7

RATING: 7.25
Traded to JF for Caylus
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.25
On the surface this might seem like a typical drafting or deck-builder, but Seasons is different.  Each player starts with 9 cards (there are a few ways to do that), and then split them across three years at the start.  After that, you work with the cards you have and hope to potentially get more.

Players try to play these cards by leveraging elements they collect each season.  Dice are rolled, and each player gets to pick one and reap those benefits.  Dice might give away elements, crystals (VPs), or cards.  Another option will be to "transmute" elements that are hard to find that season to get extra crystals.

This was so easy to pick up, we both definitely liked it, and I look forward to trying it again soon! Love the components (except that small score track), love the art (lots of great cards to enjoy), and love the concept. This is a game we picked up because it seemed unlike anything else we have, and we were right. Just unique enough to be a new winner for 2012, and certainly ripe for expansions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
After more than 75 online plays of Seasons (on Board Game Arena) I'm saying goodbye to the game for good. I gave it more than enough time to grow on me. But it didn't.

Even with the software doing much of the fiddly work (calculating and tracking the points, exchanging energy, and enforcing the MANY card interactions), at the end of a game I always felt like I had just finished an accounting test. That's not how I want to feel when I finish a game.

While it's fun to pull off a great combo, there's too much time spent waiting for your opponent to figure out how they'll maximize their play. And there were games when I felt stuck waiting for the game to just end. In fact, there are cards and tactics that let you deny your opponent playing cards. Blocking the effect of a card is one thing, but keeping them from playing cards in the first place...how is that fun?

The game seems to be at it's best as a 2-player game. But ultimately, the design of a few of the card abilities and the restricted summoning slots is what killed it for me. To have control of the game you have to spend too much effort memorizing which cards your opponent has in their hand. You have to spend an equal amount of energy checking the interactions between your cards, your opponent's cards, and the season dial. I can only imagine what it would be like without the software, but I'll never inflict that on myself.

Instead of playing Seasons, I'll reach for Star Realms when I want to play a two-player game with fun card combos. It packs more fun into a shorter game and it doesn't suffer from imbalanced card mechanics.

RATING: 7.4
Secret Santa 2013
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Components: Wonderfully chunky dice. Gorgeous, mesmerizing artwork on the cards. The cards lack a linen finish, and so are a bit dull and difficult to deal out. The season track is a bit wonky, in that the price of crystals at each of the three levels obscures the other information. The score track is a pain, because it has an inconsistent number of points per row. The theme (aside from the artwork) is silly: “You are wizards playing a game; this is that game.” A game about a game?

Experience: Uneven, both in terms of luck, and how much fun I have each turn. The dice introduce a random element that can be very damning to the player who doesn't pick first. If only one star or card are rolled, the first person to pick has a large advantage. The game is too short and the die rolls too erratically in demand for the odds to even out over the course of the game.

On my turn, it's great fun when I'm getting resources I need, and I can play one or more cool cards from my hand. Playing cards is almost always fun. But this seems to be overloaded in winter, when I typically have enough resources left over from the previous year to play every card in my hand. Then I just sit around for the other three seasons, gathering resources (sometimes just wasting them if I'm full), hoping to get an extra card, but mostly just waiting for winter to give me more cards. Thematically, it doesn't make sense that all the activity happens in winter, and we're just sitting around the rest of the time. And in terms of fun, it means that the game is fun only 25% of my turns.

The cards fall along a wide spectrum of extremely useful recurring powers (a player will be at a huge disadvantage if they don't obtain a discount-giving card), fun one-time powers, uber-powerful one-time powers, and super nasty cards. I'd advise players to familiarize themselves with the deck so they can prepare themselves emotionally for what the opponent might throw at them, or how quickly the point totals might swing.

Overall, the game is fun, but very luck dependent and sometimes unsatisfying.

First Played: 2013-06-11
Last Played: 2015-01-17
Plays (5):
2 players: 5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Seasons has great artwork, chunky dice, and card drafting (one of my favorite mechanisms). I really enjoyed this game with my first few plays while I was learning the cards and combos. In fact I would say this game is fantastic during the first 10 or so plays.

What I've found is that there's not near as much engine building as I had hoped and the deck can get pretty diluted especially with expansions. But my main beef is the BOOKKEEPING!!! You will feel like an accountant after playing a game of Seasons. Between dealing with all the card interactions, managing your summoning gauge, managing your energy, keeping up with all the point tracking on that terrible terrible scoreboard you will feel like you're working instead of playing a game sometimes. 

I really think this game is much better suited in an app form.

Also, the game can get pretty mean which will turn off some people considering there's not much interaction in the game except for those few "mean" cards. Those "mean" cards feel really really bad too. It can feel frustrating at times.

Despite all this I think there's a good game here with unique and interesting mechanics but I'm finding it hard to bring to the table when games like 51st State and Race for the Galaxy exist.

RATING: 7

I like this game so much I built my own custom insert out of foamcore.  The original insert is pretty awesome, but after the second expansion, there simply wasn't enough room for all the cards.  I also decided to sleeve this game, even though I'm not a big sleever, as the cards were starting to show a little wear.  Since I've only been using the basic cards to play, I didn't want them to wear unevenly.

RATING: 7.5
[2013-05-29 Rating: n.a. -> 7.5]

Ever since discovering Collectible Card Games (CCGs) some time ago, I'm in love with the concept of card combos. It's immensely satisfying to build a deck with some combo in mind and pull it off later. But in order to get there, you need to invest time into learning the card pool of the CCG of your choice and, perhaps more important, you need to find opponents who also want to invest time into the game. This proves to become harder and harder for me these days. So when I read Seasons' description, I thought I had found a game which could be played in a more casual way and that could still scratch that card combo itch. Since there are only 50 different cards, the card pool isn't that big and you only get dealt a fraction of it at the start of the game in the drafting phase when you're setting up your strategy. 

Until now, my plan has worked and I've found an enjoyable card combo game that isn't that hard to understand. Some additional thoughts (all based on 2 player games):

* Seasons is more of a victory point/tableau builder than a fighting card game a la Warhammer Invasion. So in year 3, there might be some AP when you're trying to max your victory points.

* Depending on the set of cards that is dealt at the beginning of the game, Seasons might play better or worse. Like in Dominion, you might just get that boring set up or the cards that you're dealt are just perfect for a fun round.

* I find the victory point adjusting every round a little fiddly. I often tend to forget that ongoing effect that gives me x victory points.

RATING: 6
Setting up for this game and listening to the explanation, I thought I would really like this game.  It seemed to have many things I like about Magic: The Gathering.   However, after playing a couple of rounds I started getting a hollow feeling about it.  It lacked a lot of interesting decisions.  There were instances where you played your cards out and just had to wait around for the year to end to get more.  Only 1 in 6 die faces allows you to draw.  So it can fizzle out and get boring.

It just seemed to me not to have anywhere near the depth as Magic.  Granted we played beginner with only cards 1-30 in play and pre-arranged decks (no drafting).  But given what I've seen thus far, I can't see it going up much higher with more complex cards + drafting.  It's just too shallow.  Your best hope is to have fun with some combo...but it's not enough.

Tastes like artificial sweetner.  I guess I may be spoiled by my many years of playing Magic.

RATING: 6
Players are wizards duelling through the seasons over three years.  Attractive, and simple game.  Players roll a bunch of chunky dice, the colours matching the current season, then proceed to draft one of them that will dictate their actions for the round.  Typically, you will gain energy in four colours, used to summon cards from your hand, to get a victory point engine going.  Works well, and the different energy types cleverly go through varying stages of value.  All in all, quite good with two, but rather stodgy with four.  Surprised at how light it was.... not a lot of thinking required.  Lots of bits of other games bolted in to create this one.  At the moment, the jury is out.

RATING: 10
2-en próbáltuk ki, s már most látszik, hogy többen jobb lehet, mert jópár kártya úgy nyer értelmet. Viszont többen pedig megnő a holtidő, hiszen egy játékos a saját körében végrehajtja az összes akcióját, ami lehet a kiválasztott kockán lévő egy vagy több akció végrehajtása, kártya kijátszása/aktivizálása, bónusz akció(k) végrehajtása. A sok gondolkodást a különböző kártyalapokban rejlő kombinációs lehetőségek maximális kihasználása adja, illetve hogyan szerezzük meg a kijátszásukhoz/aktivizálásukhoz szükséges energiaforrásokat. A játék egy "draftolási" mechanizmussal kezdődik (lásd 7 csoda), mely során kiválasztjuk a kezdő 9 lapos készletünket, ehhez nem baj, ha már ismerjük a lapok képességeit. A készítők ezért ügyesen azt találták ki, hogy ez a fázis kikerülhető előre összeállítható kis paklikkal, amik közül választunk egyet. Így egy fajta fokozatosságot biztosítva a játék megismeréséhez elkerülendő azt a fajta tanácstalanságot, amit mi leműveltünk :), mondván mit nekünk a kezdő fokozat, egyből a legnehezebbel kezdtünk, ahol az összes kártyalap játszik. Úgy választottuk ki a kezdő 9 lapot, hogy csak sejtettük, melyik mire jó. Persze menet közben kiderült, hogyan kellett volna összeállítani :). Nem baj, legközelebb jobban fog menni. Nagyon tetszett az, hogy az idő múlását a ki nem választott kockán lévő pöttyök határozzák meg. A szabályok elég könnyen érthetőek, csak a kombinációs lehetőségek felmérése okozhat egy kis problémát, egyébként alkalmas családi játéknak is. Nekem nagyon tetszett, kíváncsi vagyok, hogy ennyi (2x50) kártyalappal milyen kombinációs lehetőségeket lehet kihozni. (2015.06.10.)
Most épp lelkesedem a játékért. Épp olyan hosszúságú, ami alkalmassá teszi egy családi játéknak.Az újrajátszhatóságot a sokféle lap biztosítja. Két játékosnál a narancssárga lapok hatása nem annyira érvényesül, a lila lapok ilyenkor értékesebbek. A kulcs, hogy már a legelején jól állítsuk össze a 9 lapunkat. Jó érzés, ha egy-egy előre eltervezett kombináció bejön és sok győzelmi pontot szerzünk vele. Kíváncsi leszek, hogy több játékos esetén az egymásnak keresztbe tevés mennyire lesz befolyásoló tényező az előre tervezésnél. (2015.06.16.)

Az energiajelek a megidézésekhez kellenek, illetve a már megidézettek aktiválásához, az eladással lehet "pénzre" azaz kristályra váltani az energiakorongjainkat, a megidézési csillag növeli a megidézési képességünk. 
Alapban ez 0. Így amíg nem szerzünk csillagot, nem tudunk leidézni lapot, ami pedig nem árt, mert van 3x3 lapunk, amit az elején megkapunk és szétosztunk a 3 évünkre. Minden évben az odatervezett lapokat megkapjuk az év elején a még a kezünkbe lévőkhöz. Ha a játék végén kezünkben marad lap: mínusz pont. tehát le kell idézni őket. Na meg az arra is jó, h mindenfélékhez jutunk, egyszeri dolgokhoz, aktiválható dolgokhoz, és folyamatosan jelenlévő dolgokhoz is. 
Az évszakok kockáink ugyanazok a jelek, de más más gyakorisággal. pl Télen nincs fa. Víz és tűz meg gyakori
Összességében nagyon tetszett, könnyedebb játék, jól összerakva, jól használja a kockákat, a kártyákkal nagyon jó kombók hozhatóak létre, gyors és izgalmas.

RATING: 9
[thread=832767][/thread]

This was a review I wrote after a single play.  I have continued to play this and enjoy it.  I'll do an update on what I think about the components after I own the physical copy of the game.

Edit:  Components...
-Like the big dice
-Dislike the card backs but I guess it's better than some
-Score track sucks (I use poker chips)
-Awesome insert (fits my sleeved cards just fine)
-Insert fits all of the first and second expansions with sleeved cards too!

This game has largely replaced Race for the Galaxy and Gosu as my top 2-player game of choice.

Buy it!

--- 

Comments I made elsewhere which I'll copy/paste:

Beautiful to behold and a wonderful game experience** as well. 

What do I love about it?

-Some of the most wonderful fantasy artwork I've seen in years.

-A card drafting game with an actual game attached (7 Wonders and Fairy Tale just didn't work for me). Some would argue the draft is the game but I disagree as people will often draw into multiple cards other than what they've drafted. Tempo is important. Forward thought of what year to draw your cards matter.

-Other than the scoreboard this game has amazing components. Not many game inserts accommodate sleeved cards. Those big chunky engraved dice are wonderful. Just be sure to use poker chips or something similar instead the scoreboard.

-There is a deep game experience in here. New players will usually be beaten by experienced players, which I feel is how it should be.

-I find the experience of Seasons to be wildly varied from game-to-game. Part of it is the mix of cards in the beginning draft. Sometimes people won't roll many symbols to increase their summoning gauge. Sometimes the tempo will be slower or faster than average based on what's rolled but also how the players choose to influence it. There can be a huge disparity of score from game to game. I've seen winning games with a paltry 75-ish points to other games where someone has about 250 points. This makes close games all the more tense. It's also the reason I've played this game over 100 in the past 6 months.

-I'm happy that this is not a multiplayer solitare game. That said, there aren't so many directly confrontational cards that it feels like a 'take that' card game. It has just the right amount of interaction for my tastes.

-I feel this game is more varied and better balanced w/ different strategies to pursue than many of my favorite card games base sets*** (that includes Race for the Galaxy, Ascension, and Gosu). There are 2 cards I consider problematic (temporal boots - too good, balance of ishtar - too weak) but Balance of Ishtar and Idol of the Familiar were re-balanced from the first edition. Temporal Boots is still too good. 

I feel like everyone should try this game. Thankfully people have the opportunity to do so for free at the BGA website.

**I pretty much exclusive play this with only 2 players and feel the experience get's worse with the more players you add. 3 is still a decent game, but I won't even consider playing with 4.

***There used to be card games I prefer to Seasons but if I had to play just the base set of any of those card games, I would probably prefer to play Seasons.

RATING: 7
I have a feeling that this is going to settle into a 6-7.  My initial thoughts are that the cards aren't super balanced.  And I always do poorly at games where I have to keep up on the text of a dozen cards in front of me and gain rewards or dole penalties based on various conditions written on the card.  It's too frustrating to keep forgetting to take my bonuses and either potentially lose as a result or feel like I'm cheating to request them after the fact.

That said, I do like the fact that the cards are limited to 9 for the game (broken out 3 at a time), plus draws, and that you have to have sufficient summoning strength.  So it's not a total card fest till the end of the game.

RATING: 8
[b]Rating based on - 1000+ plays, 2 player - 3 player - 4 player
Preferred player Count: 2 (sometimes 3)[/b]

No, that is not a typo. I have played this game over 1000 times. In addition to owning and playing it in real life, I play a lot on Board Game Arena. The interplay of cards is totally fascinating to me and some of the combos you can make are awesome. Replayability? Oh yes! In Spades. Where this game fails for me is the double card effect. You get somebody who has 2 dice of Malice and will re-roll every single turn, plus 2 Wondrous Chests and they are sitting on 10 points a turn. They don't play cards, they just sit on points *YAWN* Games are really boring then. In addition, if you have each opponent in a 3 player game with a Karin the Destroyer (or one player with both) and a good supply of energy tokens you can be decimated pretty quickly. Some cards can be used to great effect, some can be a bit lame. I very rarely see any use for the Beggar's Horn except its crystal point value. Also, cards are the soul of this game. The only way to get them is by dice roll. Sometimes you are sitting there with lots of summoning gauge and no cards come up (or your opponent takes them and re-rolls them), sometimes vice versa. For normal point optimisation goodness I play in person. Brutal, cutthroat and aggressive play is on BGA...just depends on what I'm in the mood for.

RATING: 5
Initially I really enjoyed the game idea, colors, and graphics. I thinked I could have fun imagining the strategies and learning the different cards combos...
Then I played 3-4 games, and I thinked I was understanding it, and had still some fun in figuring combos... but it seemed a bit too slow for me and a little boring to wait other player/s turn.
Then I played some other games and...bang it got REALLY BORING. Turn after turn just collecting resources, and waiting to get the right die before the enemy. Then wait minutes for a clever opponent to make combo combo, take this down, this up this down, and after 30 minutes of combo he has won by 3 points because you had been so bored to death that you forgot to use a power of one of your cards.
Or wait turns to draw a card because you don't ever get the good die?

Nah, this game needed 1 year more of development. It COULD have been a nice game, but with SEVERAL modifications.
As it stands, it's too much boring to mind playing. If I get an offer to play it by a friend who likes it, I will play, else it will not find space on my gametable, sorry!

RATING: 6.8
[b]Sold[/b]
We liked Seasons a lot when we first got it, but went back to the game more recently, and without the familiarity with the card pool fresh in our minds, the game lost a lot.  We also confirmed that it was way less fun with more than two players, so didn't see it getting played often enough to keep. Of the games I've gotten rid of, Seasons was one of the tougher decisions - it's a solid game that I played a fair bit, but just didn't think I would play much anymore.
[b]previous comment:[/b]

I am usually not a big fan of draft-up-front in my games.  I don't like the feeling that I pretty much had the game lost before it started, because I chose poorly on the cards.  However, Seasons has enough variety, especially with the first expansion added, that I still enjoy it.  I like the variety of different paths to victory, and the way you can try to build an engine out of cards that synergize well.  I also really like the N+1 dice drafting mechanic.  This isn't a game I will necessarily always be quick to pull out, and I definitely feel it works best with two, but it's a good solid game.

RATING: 7
Two three player games before rating it. It has a few presentation issues that could be a bit more friendly - bigger text, bigger spaces for the cubes.   Almost felt like Magic meets 7 Wonders meets Dominion but then there are the dice as well.  We played again straight away after the first " learning game".  Second game took 75 mins. RATING: 7
After a single game this feels very clunky. Non of the actions seem to flow once you begin gameplay (the draft portion is second nature having played both 7wonders and MtG) and the initial game is very slow as you desperately try to get stars to be allowed to play cards.

Jumped straight in at the advanced game which was probably a mistake as we had a non-gamer join us at the last minute as a 4th player. This may have contributed to the clunky feel of the game.

Art work is stunning and the flavour of the game shines through however the theme could have been anything.

I hope there is more ways in which you can interact with your opponents i.e. bouncing cards back to hands or making them draw more cards, not just taxing them for actions. Familiars seem more powerful than magic items but that could have been because one player focused on familiars alone.

I think this is the kind of thing I was hoping for with quarriors where you are drafting a limited pool  of dice.

I also hope the clunky-ness was due to it being the first game we played and thus will diminish with more player, but I am not certain it will.

RATING: 6
Rating history 8|8|6

:star::star::star::nostar::nostar: - Current rating.
PRO: short duration, nice graphics/components, drafting
CON: combos and powers are very straightforward/simple

There's a lot I should like in this game that I don't get from a lot of other games. I enjoy drafting, and this game has a simple 9-card draft. I enjoy dividing cards into prioritized piles (a very underused mechanic!). Combo-making is a favorite of mine. The art in this game is also nice.

But it's flat.

This game suffers compared to other "combo-making" games I like. There are a lot of them these days: Imperial Settlers, Deus, Impulse, and to a lesser extend Agricola, Le Havre, etc. Season catches the eye with good graphics, but delivers an overly simple game for my tastes. This is a great game to play with people new to combo games and card activations, but for me it's just not enough.

RATING: 6
I had to re-read the directions on this game more than any other.  They're not actually that confusing, especially after you realize that half the "boards" you use are just there for keeping track of score, various point systems, or "time".  There's just a lot of minutia to understand, and strategy often works around it, so you can't just check a rule while in the middle of play.

Lots of different cards to choose from and lots of different strategies to try, so it has good replay-ability.  There's dice, but they're not so central that RNG-haters would be put off by it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Pros
-Decent amalgamation of many different mechanics
-In-game actions make (some) thematic sense
-Game feels like a good length (and players can control it to some degree)
-Players can form a strategy from what they have in their hand and they know what is coming up later in the game due to drafting of starting cards
-LARGE unique dice

Cons
-Some swingy game moves/combos (e.g. look at next card of deck, gain mana equal to its cost, which can be from 0 to 7/max)
-Score board is very small, and score changes VERY often
-Feels like it could use some more variation (i.e. the game only two categories of cards - items and familiar)
-A lot of abilities that screw your opponents over and reduce their VP. For example, I ended my second game with 0 VP (but I still got points that couldn't be reduced from my other cards), and the score board goes up to 300.
-Individual cards (art) and theme is not memorable, nothing really holds it together and overall theme feels slapped on.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Seasons has many of the qualities I despise in Dominion and then adds some more of its own: Turns that last anywhere from 1 second to upwards of 5 minutes, a game that - while not necessarily decided - is very much set on its tracks immediately after the initial setup but goes on for very long, lots of different text-heavy cards to try to build combos with, too much downtime, and lots of specific card effects I don't particularly care about.

The dice drafting sounded quite interesting but turned out to be a fairly mundane affair. Some of my problems with the game would get better with mutiple plays I'm sure but the rest is sufficiently unpleasant that I'm not interested in investing that much time. The short version: Not my game at all.

RATING: 8.1
Good card game with a lot of interesting mechanics. Too many interesting mechanics when you first start playing, but they are all fun once you get it.

My one complaint seems to agree with many others here: the bulk of the game is drafting your cards and choosing which pile to put them in. After that (the first few minutes of the game) you're largely spending an hour seeing how those decisions play out. By the end of our games we're usually begging for more cards and swimming in elements. This hurts what would otherwise be a fantastic game. It doesn't happen every time, but it happens often enough.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
A gaming buddy facetiously mentioned that he really wanted me to try Seasons. And why not! It's got almost everything I typically avoid in games: Text-heavy card drafting, tableau building in relative isolation, combos left and right, family-friendly graphic design. Hell yeah! 

So I sat down with this buddy who has been playing the game actively online and another friend, and started drafting pretty much blind. I got the two cards that made others give me a point every time they summoned a card, the one that made them give me a point every time the season changed, and the one that allowed me to discard an energy to make others lose 4pts. Oh, and the die re-roll one. For the first half of the game or so, I was well up the VP chart while the other two were at 0 or single digits. And then I won. Fucking ridiculous. 

Downtime when playing with more than just two can be painful.

RATING: 7.5
Not the quick, addictive card game that I was expecting. Plays more slowly than Dominion, 7 Wonders and Race for the Galaxy.  However, it is when you play online!!  Rating is 8 for online play.  Probably down to a 7 when playing a cardboard version.

However, the opportunity for comboing is immense (might be that there are better combos here than in the above). Drafting is always amazing. Short and long term planning is useful, always balancing the immediate points grab with the slow buildup of summoned power cards.

Unfortunately, exploring the cards is more entertaining than mastering the combos. That, I think, is why people feel the game is short lived (with only 50 unique power cards and 20-25 coming out in a 2p game). If more decks are designed for the game, I would be very interested as the system is quite enjoyable (but only as good as the cards that have been designed for it).

Rating dropped for 2 reasons:
1) Takes far too long to play in person. I only play on BoardGameArena now.
2) The deck gets old very quickly, as suspected. The same combos are used from game to game.

RATING: 5
nice artwork, interesting cards to work with.  

the use of theme is decent - it feels like you are casting spells.

a few large problems for me though:

- player interaction is pretty limited; so it isn't my kind of game.  yes, your cards and the dice you take sometimes affect the other players, but you have to play the cards you have, and you are going to take the dice that work for your cards.

- IMHO, all of the interesting aspects of this game happen at the beginning with the draft and the assignment of the cards to the 3 phases.  This is bad for beginning or casual players.  It is also bad for pacing; the climax of the game is going to depend on a bunch of luck-based things that happen long after you have committed to a course of action.

- the actual score of who is winning is not tracked.  Unless you go to the tedious task of adding up everyone's cards every turn, you don't know who is winning.  Since the card info is open, the VP should be tracked.

- I'm not sure that adding players adds to the game.  It probably works way better as a fast two player game, than an hour or two long four player game.

RATING: 10
I initially bought this because of its two-player sweet spot, for my sister and I to play. We both love the game, but to my surprise, so does our mother! She was attracted by the game laid out on the table and persuaded to join in on a game. 

We now play as many three-player as two-player games and I like both. The two-player game is and feels quicker; a three-player game is longer, but I can enjoy the slower pace and like watching the other players play their cards.

In many ways this game reminds me of Catan Card Game, which I like, but I like Seasons much better. So if you like Catan Card Game, I'd say you'll like Seasons. 
In both games you use resources to buy cards, which, all in their own way, earn you points. In Catan Card Game your resources get dictated by the dice, whereas in Seasons you can always choose between a minimum of two dice, allowing a better fit for your cards.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.25
The game is good. Interesting choices, yet casual feeling. Great artwork.

Drafting phase is fun with combo/synergy-hunting, overall cost balancing and planning.

The game cleverly forces players to divide the drafted nine cards into starting hand and two 3-card batches which are acquired later in the game. This makes game flow smoothly as there is less possibilities between which cards to play during the 'tournament', the actual playing phase the game.

The different resource type distributions and conversion rates to VPs between different seasons add nice planning, timing and risk-taking element into the game. The seasons/years circle is also a good intuitive way to represent the timeline of the game.

The length of the game is ideal, not too short not too long. There is great variety between games, because of the sizable pool of cards. Also the card effects are well designed, varied and offer interesting combinations and synergies to watch for.

The bonus actions make the game a lot of more forgiving and dampens a bit the randomness of the dice. The draw a card effect of the dice is really good as it opens the game a bit for more uncertainty.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
In ZRH-EURA (locked)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Seasons is primarily a card game, with drafting and hand management being the primary keys to success. Each player will draft a 9-card hand, then split it into 3 piles of 3, one for each year in the game. These cards generally have costs that must be paid in resources in order to get the benefits they offer (which almost always includes victory points). The resources themselves come from the dice. Each round, the starting player rolls the dice and picks one of them. Each player in turn order also selects one. These dice provide the resources needed to pay for the cards. 

The cards have some duplication, which is good for familiarity in drafting, but also good in the sense that multiple copies can sometimes really help a certain strategy. It seems that there are a lot of different paths to victory, with plenty of room for adaptation. This flexibility and broad strategic scope are really admirable given the relatively small amount of cards. Unfortunately, it seems this game plays better with fewer players. With the full complement of four, accidental chaos is a big problem. It is very easy to accidentally get in the way of other players' goals simply by pursuing your own, not to mention the fact that there are quite a few harshly interactive cards. It's still fun with more players, but it won't reward long-term planning quite as well.

The dice and cards are good quality, nicely illustrated. Unfortunately, the rules are ambiguous about certain timing issues and whether or not certain abilities are mandatory. The scoring track is pitifully small and easily bumped. The terminology is sometimes confusing and alternates inexplicably between symbols and the actual term in the card text. These are generally minor, but it still seems oddly sloppy in what is an otherwise very polished game. 

All in all, Seasons seems like it could really have legs and combines two underused mechanics (drafting and dice selection) into a very interactive hand management game that should appeal to eurogamers and CCG players alike. Nevertheless, like so many CCGs, it seems at its best when played 1 on 1.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Hey, whaddya know, this is actually really fun. Some cards seem to be considerably stronger than others, but most of the time creative play and drafting will take care of that. The pieces are a little "floaty" - so don't bump the table.

Drafting covers the player interaction.  Unique theme in that you are battling for "years".  Downtime can be long, but that's only a problem if you don't like it.  I don't mind downtime or AP - tells me i'm getting a good game from the other person and they are having fun.

     At first thought, most of the strategy comes from the drafting at the beginning of the game, but two things come into play during the second phase : the high interaction with the other players through the dice and the timing needed to gain the right energy tokens(when and which dice to take also have a big affect on this).  Which cards are in the draft pool does come down to luck, but I think some gamers who will put this game down as a 'luckfest' need to learn a hard lesson : sometimes it's the better thing to do to sacrifice a card you may want in order to keep your opponent from getting a card they need. It is going to be difficult to block your opponent well while gaining crystals yourself.  

     Negative : The blandness of the card effects is completely disappointing.  Like I say below, no cards are broken, but on a whole they are too powerful. An expansion that adds more depth seems necessary.  

     Also, this is nothing like MTG. There are also no broken or too powerful cards.  If someone tells you either of these two things, stop listening to their advice.

Edit : Couple hours after first play and still thinking about how I could do better.  

Edit : second play - It's just a fun game that you will enjoy.  Play with two players and you get a nice 30m to 45m game.

Edit : Good with four players also.

Edit : great game.

RATING: 7.5
Seasons is a slick little card game, reminding me (at least a little bit) of MtG.

The game is full of colorful artwork, nicely designed packaging for the bits, and some of the most popular (and sizable) dice to ever be seen on BGG.  The dice are used to generate available actions- always one more die than #players, so there are a set of randomized options each round.

Basically the game is a contest set over 3 years, divided by months but also by three month long seasons. In each season the power of some of the 4 elements is more or less plentiful, and this cycles around predictably. There may be an opportunity to cache that magical power as crystals- and the more scarce an elemental power the more crystals can be formed of it.

Crystals are sometimes used as a commodity in the game, but they are also simply VPs for the game-end.

Of course, player-sorcerers may also need those crystals to summom magic items or familiars- and you either need a source for rare power or need to save/collect it for that use sometimes. In addition to special effects (1x or Multi-use) Magic items and faniliars are also generally worth some VP at game end, and this is perhaps 
the more effective way of gaining Crystals/VPs.

The game is set with a multi-player solitaire deck of 30 cards (2x for each card), but also includes a far more interactive set of 20 cards (2x for each card) once the game is learned.

Each player starts with 9 cards, and then a card draft is run where players select a single card each round. Players then set aside 3 cards for both the 2nd and the 3rd years, and start with 3 cards in-hand.

At this point I've played about 3 games with varying counts, all with the less interactive card set. I think the game is slick enough to be fun even with the basic deck, and I expect it will improve with the interactive cards. I'm starting this at a 7.25- it's a nice little production with superior production values, and it's not out to separate you from your hard-won cash like Collectors' or Living Card games (though there IS an expansion on the way already...).

Increased to a 7.5 after playing w Interactive cards.

RATING: 9
“Winter is coming.” -Eddard Stark

GAMEPLAY
Players are the mages of Xidit come together to show off their powers to become the archmage. Each turn the starting player rolls special dice to determine what energies are available for the wizards to craft their items. The Dice are specific to each season and have more or less energy symbols depending on the season. The dice energies have one or two winter, spring, summer, or fall and sometimes one of two different seasons. In addition the dice may indicate that the player can play more power cards, gain a power card, gains crystals, or can transmute energy into crystals. The power cards build the mages’ capabilities. Some powers are simple, use two winter energy to get 20 crystals. Some powers rely on the opponent’s resources, spend two autumn energy to copy an opponent’s energy pool and add it to your own. Some powers make it easier for the mage, spend one energy of each type and for the rest of the game calling powers takes one less energy. The mages look to play as many power cards as possible as they add to the victory point total in addition to their effects. The game is broken down into three years and each year into 12 months. The turns move faster or slower depending on the power dice remaining from the turns’ roll. There are two copies of fifty different power cards in the game and the rules recommend using only the first 30 for the first few play throughs as the effects of the last 20 are more complicated and interact in with each other more. With so many powers there is a lot of replay-ability. At the end of the third year each player totals played powers and crystals, the mage with the most points wins the title of Archmage.

COMPONENTS
The card board elements of the game are the good standard, gamers have come to expect from Asmodee. The energy tokens fit into the top of each player board and the symbols all clearly indicate what they are. The dice are much larger than standard size, so aggressive dice rolling should be avoided. The artwork is top notch with interesting details on the player board and the power cards. There are a lot of colors in play because blue, green, yellow, and red are used for the seasons and player colors are orange, grey, brown, and purple.

THEME
I don’t think the world of Xidit has shown up anywhere else. So this new generic magical world has more exploring to be done in it. Everything that has been presented in this box fits and builds a unique high fantasy world. The flow of time on the circular time board feels smooth and is very well implemented into gameplay. The game turns are fast and building power divided by the mages makes for interesting game choices.

WHO IS IT FOR?
This game can cover a wide range of gamers. Those as young as ten can handle Seasons and because of its short play time, under an hour, will work great for families. Seasons also works well for heavier gamers as there are tons of possibilities with 50 different power cards in the game. The game plays 2 to 4 and more players offers more interaction for more interesting gameplay.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Drop-dead gorgeous production values slathered over a so-so apparatus.  After two plays I'm into it and looking forward to more, but will henceforth heed the common warning that 4p is just too much.  Downtime was brutal and who knows, maybe it picks up with familiarity but I'm not interested in finding out.

It feels like an 8 but I'm gonna make [i]Seasons[/i] work for it.

Also:  Big chunky dice FTW!

[b]After 4 plays:[/b]  I'm pretty sure this is just a 2p experience.  Even with only 3p the downtime during two consecutive super-turns (with card play and effects chaining on and on and on...) is an enthusiasm killer.  Especially when my stupid turn is "I gain two energy.  Next!" followed by two more super-turns.  [i]Gaaah.[/i]

[b]After 6 plays:[/b]  It's an 8.  Play time's picking up as we become more familiar with the cards and we haven't even cracked the "advanced" set of 20.  Just plain friendly and appealing.  What can I say?  It's... [i]nice[/i]... like a warm, French bubble bath.  I can soak.

UPDATE:  [i]I slipped on the Temporal Boots, thinking I was all kinds of clever—only to find myself sprinting backwards, screaming, into the Port-A-Potty to suck yesterday's dump up through the hole.[/i]

RATING: 6.9
I wasn't 100% about this purchase, so I was tentative when I did my first solo play test of it to learn the rules. I found it dull and too deterministic. Then I played it with my wife. Before the game started we realized I had made a mistake: The cards you draft at the start of the game are not the only ones. A 'draw' action is from the deck with the rest of the cards, not from upcoming years. No clue why I thought that. That really changed things as new power cards can come into play. My second mistake was to underestimate how much a second player would add to the game that I could never replicate by playing both players in my play testing. In the end, I find this game to be fun and we are always surprised that the game lasts us 50 minutes or so because it feels much faster than that. Very engaging.

RATING: 10
The interaction between cardplay and resource management is like candy it's so immediately rewarding, flavorful, and addictive. And I cannot say enough about the artwork, which is some of the most dazzling, gorgeous imagery I've seen since Omen a Reign of War. Seasons has a "light" theme, but it certainly integrates itself well with the mechanics.

We used the prebuilt beginner decks, and all of us immediately picked up on the synergies between cards. With only one of us having played even once, I was afraid Seasons might drag. It didn't.  It picked up right away, and with little to no downtime steamrolled right to the end. I used crystal beads to replace the scoring track, and this made the management of collecting, stealing, and spending them infinitely more intuitive and natural, and likely sped up the game. 
2P: It works surprisingly well with two. Playtime is an hour or less.
3P: This game's sweetspot. Perfects the player interaction and game length.
4P: If players don't overanalyze their turns it can work, otherwise it stretches a relatively light game into an uncomfortably long experience.

RATING: 3.5
This game does a lot of things well, but unfortunately is let down by some major problems:

1)A lot of the cards add some serious fiddlyness to the vp track during a turn or at the end of a round/season

2)the game can be very slow, and dull when it's not your turn

3)getting points early on can be good in some games, but in others (if other players have drafted vp taxing cards) they can be useless

4)the draft at the start is the most important part of the game, if you do badly through bad luck or not getting any good combos then it's game over unless you get lucky with card draw (from dice or cards) later in the game

5)there are too many useless cards in the deck which you may be forced to take in the draft or draw during the game

RATING: 5
Seasons has wonderful art, great components, and interesting mechanics.

Where the game loses me is with its collectible game-style card interactions. Toward the end of the game, there are too many interactions and effects to try and remember.

Additionally, many of the powerful combinations aren't initially apparent, making this a game where one can almost guarantee losing in the game's initial card draft.

There's much I like about Seasons, but it doesn't have the kind of depth I am looking for in a board game.

RATING: 7
Seasons is one of those games that is deceivingly simple at the outset, but which reveals more layers the more a person plays.  Players try to collect the most crystals, all the while building their summoning powers to play cards that help them gain even more crystals, or cause other players to lose crystals.  The unique dice, the simple setup, the quick game play, the back and forth nature of the cards, and replayability make this a keeper.  One of the other good things about Seasons is that it plays equally good at 2, 3, and 4 players.  The artwork is a little cheesy for me.  I think it would have worked better with a classic, dungeons & dragons type theme, but I can respect the designers were trying for something more unique.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

The resource management is also very interesting as you can essentially sell resources during other seasons where they might be more scarce for a bit of an extra bonus.

Initial Rating: 6.0 (February 2013)

At first I didn’t like the game very much, I thought it was a regular game when I played the apprentice mode without the draft, however, with the draft this game is easily a 7.0 for me, a good game I’m usually willing to play. I love card games and this is a very good card game. The art is gorgeous and the game components are great. 

The rules are fairly easy to get, but the game has some interesting decisions from beginning to end. The game is a little light for my taste, but I do like it.
 
For me, Seasons is played best with 2 players, fun with 3 players. With 4 players the downtime is excessive for me so I won’t play it that way. I plan to buy it in the near future.

RATING: 7
I got Seasons after playing Dice Forge, which is a great game from the same author. Being a Magic fan, I found Seasons to be quite classical in its mechanisms: time goes by, you get to roll dice and you invoke magical objects with effects using energy tokens. It plays really nicely, although it's a bit long (this is why it's best with 2 players). I customized the deck, as some cards seemed over-powered or unbalanced for a 2-player game. I am planning to buy expansions in the future (the box seems to have plenty of space for them!) which might make the game more intense.

RATING: 7.5
Wow, two plays in (3 players each time) and I'm blown away by how much fun this is. Look past the Magic-style jargon and the gameplay is actually pretty simple, but there are a lot of choices in play, a reasonable amount of interaction for a Euro and just enough of a random element from the dice to avoid 100% predictability without it degenerating into utter chaos.

Stunning looks (especially if you pimp it up with a actual crystals for scoring), and the central interaction between the dice and the season wheel is unique and very fun.

As others have said I'd avoid playing with 4 to avoid excessive downtime, but for 2 of 3 it's one I'm happy to recommend.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
- This game is great, but not for everyone. It can come across as heavy-ish in weight, similar to Race for the Galaxy.
- Aesthetics and components are excellent.
- This game is all about the cards; building and executing an engine. 
- There is so much variety in the cards which makes for heaps of replay-ability, particularly if you include either of the expansions which are both pretty good. I have both but I don't think I'd like the game any less if I didn't have any. 
- The drafting at the start is so good because it allows you to decide on a strategy (somewhat) and structure your game to make sure you have particular cards available in the early, mid and late game. I wish other games like Race for the Galaxy did this.
- Symbology is clear and consistent, but there will probably be moments where you need to refer to the rule book to see how a card works, particularly in combination with another.
- Teaching is okay, but the game will probably be daunting to new players.
- This game can suffer from a runaway-leader problem as there's not much players can do to slow a single player down. From memory, all, or at least most of the take-that(ish) cards affect all other players not just one.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
After a straight up card draft to start the game, you then draft a die each turn to give you energy (to play cards), draw another card, increase your potential tableau size, and/or simply get points. Sometimes you can transmute energy into points rather than spending it on playing cards from your hand. Combinations of cards have you manipulating all of these actions, and other cards, to collect massive quantities of points in short order. The game is paced by a 12 step rondel that moves 1-3 steps per turn (dictated by the die NOT chosen), so you can also manipulate the number turns to be played as well. Different energies transmute to different amounts of points depending on where you are on the rondel.

It's a hard game on new players because of the need to draft your base hand for that entire game before you start playing. So, I should write off a few learners games before I really decide how much I like it, but the truth is I don't know if there are enough interesting decisions in-game to make it worthwhile for me. I felt a bit stuck with my pre-game draft with precious little influx of new in-game options. Your tableau can get up to 15 cards (!), which is a lot to keep track of (even 10 feels like a lot to me), and I kept feeling the urge to re-read every card every turn to make sure I wasn't forgetting anything. And I still forgot stuff. And so did my experienced opponent! Even if I respect them, I have trouble loving games that have me doubting and constantly checking and rechecking my personal tableau. I much prefer finding opportunities on a dynamically changing shared play space! Seasons is not a bad game, but I'm pretty confident it is not for me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
An interesting engine-building game, where the cards are propelled by custom dice specific to each season of the game. Much better when played with the initial drafting variant, but it also makes this game hard to teach. New players won't have much idea how the cards work together, and a random deal of nine cards won't mesh well. Once you get over this minor learning hurdle though, there's an enjoyable game to be played, with some satisfying combos thanks to a plethora of different power cards. And once everyone is familiar with the ins and outs, plays in a remarkably short span of time - making it easy to squeeze in between meatier games, or to play multiple times at a go.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I had low expectations due to the combo-building part but Seasons was a positive surprise. It's more a combination of 7 Wonders and Race for the Galaxy than the combomania I dread in Dominion. Tableau building games are the one type where I can stand engine building. Probably, because it's not so much about getting a few killer combos to play repeatedly but rather a complete working build. 
Compared to 7 Wonders, Seasons offers a broader more complex decision space with the initial draft of 9 cards that players distribute equally to the three ages. From the start on, players know almost all cards in the game and have to prepare a long-term plan. Some randomness in addition to the cards is mixed in by the dice, and in the base version a few minor targeted effects are added which are fine with me as they target all players similarly. Hopefully, the advanced version with more interactive cards beyond the initial set of 30 doesn't spoil my impression.  
While Seasons is a nice change of pace from 7 Wonders for gamers, it will be too much for occasional gamers. It's on par with Race for the Galaxy or Glory to Rome in terms of demand.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I love this game so far. Rating will rise or fall after we get into the more advanced ways to play.

It is my favorite game to play with my wife. And I spend more time gaming with her than I do with anyone. The art is top notch, as are the rest of the components. 

One complaint. The counters! Why a counter board? It looks great, but all it takes is a light bump to taint the results of such an amazing game. Still my favorite, but there must be something that I can do to avoid this happening again.

RATING: 9.3
Season is a fun experience with a beautiful sense of accomplishment. The game has an awesome mechanic for setting up how the course of the game will play out. The game only gets better when you add more cards with the expansion. My only complaint is the less involved player interaction, but I think its understandable for this type of game. 

Sessons feels like its a very skilled based game. Luck does not really play as a factor. If i lose, its due to my own decision making. If i win, I know its because i played a smart game. The game is simple to learn while having some very nuanced intelligent design. Adaption is key for victory when you are deterministically setting up your seasons. My favorite aspect of the game is the early drafting portion of the game. Developing how your cards come out during the years make your decisions feel so valuable. Your choices mean so much throughout the courses of the game. 

People complain about the theme being pasted on, but I can sense the theme while I play. I imagine myself a wizard in some forest competing for some prowess among the local wizards. At the end of the competition we meet in a pub and share a drink. The sole negative comment I can share is that the game lacks a greater sense of interaction. But that doesn't mean it is not there. The familiars add a good level of take that, but i would have loved to have seen more. Expansions add that sense of greater variety which solidifies this game as a classic on my self. 

Anyways, Seasons is a brilliant game that gives me a warm feeling inside. A relaxed experience with a great sense of complexity. I find myself looking forward to becoming the arch-mage every time I play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Very easy to learn and amazingly gripping abstract game.  Usually games with abstract themes tend to lose me a bit and I never get into it thematically leaving me a bit detached to the experience.  However, with Seasons, the gameplay carries the game enough where it makes me care about what I'm doing.  Mixing a bit of card handling and dice rolling makes the game a very distinct taste.  The game is nice in the mixture of mechanics from drafting to card play along with resource management and some take that.  Depending if you play with the full card set or the basic allows players of all levels to enjoy the game together.  The smoothness of play and the rare chance of AP locking games makes this a high choice among my games to pull out when I want to have fun.  The amazing art work, unique dice, colorful theme, all rolls into one SUPER VALUE package!  I don't know if there will be other games like it since the mechanics are so varied that it really takes an abstract game like this to pull it off.  Moderation is good, and this game mixes in everything fun about board games with enough moderation to not over do it, and to grab people enough to have them want to play it some more.  Really really good game.  Everyone should have this in their collection.

基本ドラフトゲームは合わないので辛目の採点。ドラフトゲームは基本カードの特殊効果を選択することから始まるが、それはカードの特殊効果の使いどころがわかる必要があり、それはカード全体でのそのカードの役割がある程度理解できていないとできないこと。そのため、初心者には厳しい。

RATING: 6
After a couple more plays of Seasons, I have to say that I don't find it to be fun at all. It's colorful, but the boards are horribly cramped and the theme adds nothing to the game. There is too much fiddly counting of points on the crystal track, and the game would be much improved by the inclusion of some double-sided tokens to mark the effects of the cards in play. But even this wouldn't fix the downtime, which is ultimately what kills the game for me. In a four-player game this problem renders the game unplayable, in my opinion. I would also have to agree with the reviewer who said that the fundamental way you should be scoring points (by converting energy tokens into crystals, based on the present season) is completely overshadowed by the items and familiars. I am not at all impressed.
