RATING: 8
Overall, I've been pretty impressed with this game so far. For someone that hasn't been able to hold their interest in more open deck construction like you see with Magic the Gathering, this scratches an itch. The drafting phase lets you strategize against your opponents and the seasons decks bring in some neat timing elements. Additionally, I love the seasons track/dice that bring in a bit of randomness while providing enough information and options to mitigate luck some. Loosely put, this is an interesting game, but sadly I can see my MtG playing friends frustrated with it simply for the fact it's not MtG.... Which is a shame since this is a good little design.

RATING: 7.5
Very fun game with some amazing art and colorful pieces. There's sort of an odd disconnect between phase 1, the draft, and phase 2, the dice rolling.. stuff. The draft is a lot of fun, trying to figure out what evil combos you can put together for maximum points. Then suddenly the drafting is completely over, and it completely switches gears. The luck of the dice however seems to be overshadowed by your picks in the draft. If you have much better combos than your opponents from phase 1, you will most likely trounce them in phase 2 no matter what.

It's a good game and definitely worth playing, but I feel like it could have been a better game if phase 2 was different. Either faster, or have a larger impact on the game.

RATING: 6
This is one of those games that takes one play just to learn it.  I mean, someone else can sit down and tell you how the game flows, but understanding the effects of the cards and how they all interact is going to take one game to understand.  That's not a bad thing, mind you, but it's something to take into account.

The game can be decided by wild swings in luck, even though it will take some time to build up a tableau that will allow you to draw cards, and that can be pretty frustrating.  The drafting of cards and dice helps to overcome it being simply a luckfest, but there's still some randomness from both resources.  The card combos can create a lot of chaos, too, what with the different ways that everything interacts, and while I can see that creating a lot of strategy and replayability, I'm not sure if it will be enough to overcome the frustrations one can experience during the game.

I'd play it again, but I'm glad I didn't buy it.

5 plays: 2 players
1 play: 4 players

RATING: 9
Great tableau building game with almost infinite replayability. Figuring out a way of making the most efficient use of your cards is a very neat puzzle to solve. I just wish there were more ways of digging through the deck during the game (something similar to Race for the Galaxy's "Explore +5" action would be perfect) - that way you would have much more control over your strategy (right now everything relies mostly on initial draft).

One word of warning though - I think Seasons works best with 2 players, it's too long and too chaotic with full player count as there's too much bookeeping to take care of. With more than 30 cards in play, moving all these little wooden cubes and keeping track of every special ability every round can be a real pain. The downtime also gets significantly longer. Just stick to 1v1 games and you'll be fine.

[i]I own the following expansions: Enchanted Kingdom, Path of Destiny.[/i]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
We are sorcerers in a tournament challenge all out brawl to the top of the victory point ladder. All important initial 7 wonder style spell draft determines your fate in the following card play phase. Next, we strategically divide our deck into 3 hands to be played over three phases. Elements used for spells are generated by the different seasonal dice which are drafted each turn in player turn order. The unused dice affects the passage of time--very cool mechanic. A lot of screw your neighbor, lock-you-down cards round after round. Have to play this with the right group. Steep learn curve for newbies and drafting is meanlingless to them let alone deciding which hand to put them in. My advice is to play with hands face up and ease up on the gas pedal till they get the hang of it. You will hate the player on your right by the end of this game.

RATING: 7
Super Huge THANK YOU to my Secret Santa 3013! :)

First, I would rate this game between a 7 and 8, so it is a keeper. This is a good card game with a 'euro' feel to it, which in my books is a boon.

The cards each have various abilities and aside from taking advantage of playing those abilities well, there are 'season' bits to manage that will open the way for you to play your cards and gain more points. This is a great combination of cards/euro and the fantasy theme gives it a lustrous appeal. 

This game also has the advantage of not being quite like other games, so it holds a unique position in how it plays. It is very enjoyable and I would like to thank my Secret Santa again for introducing my household to this terrific gaming experience.

RATING: 3
[i]Seasons[/i] would make a good Halloween costume, as the game's lack of development is genuinely frightening.

If you like to draft cards, play Fairy Tale or Magic: The Gathering. If you like card combo games, play Race For the Galaxy, San Juan, or Dominion.  If your expectations are lower, and all you want is a functional game, then you [i]still[/i] need to look elsewhere.  [i]Seasons[/i] doesn't fit that description either.

Like any drafting game that deserves to be despised, some cards in [i]Seasons[/i] are insane must-picks and others are worthless.  This is a critical problem when only 7-12 cards hit the table (per player) over the course of a full game.

Please deal me the broken card.  Please.

Oh, then there's the card-drawing. It's nearly impossible to draw additional cards unless you get lucky (as first player) and roll a "card draw" result.  This means there's not much to do if you've played out your hand early in the year - except to earn resources and sell them for crystals.  And as much fun as a repetitious resource/crystal exchange might sound, it isn't.

Last and least, the game's too long with four players.

My assumption is that 95% of the game budget was thrown at the card artists, and the rest went into the colored ink in the rulebook. None of the money went into playtesting, that's for sure.

RATING: 9
8 based on first play (2 players.)

Fun to play.  There's a lot more game here than you can uncover in a single play, however its easy enough to learn that you dont feel lost when you start - unlike certain card drafting games (Im lookin at YOU 7 Wonders!)

Very cool mechanics make for interesting tactical play but strategy probably takes a few plays to develop.  

Feels like theres a lot of randomness, and there is, but its far from off the rails.  The way the dice are designed and the way the card draft works means that the randomness mostly works to help replayability and doesnt really defeat strategic play.

up to 8.5 and then 9 after multiple plays with 2,3 and 4 players.  Very fun and satisfying.  Currently the house favorite game.

RATING: N/A
2-4 players draft a hand of 9 cards then lay them out in stacks of three to be available for each year. They then roll and pick dice that let them gather resources, expand their power, and use their cards for points and abilities. Resource availability changes as the seasons progress, and cards left in hand at the end of the game incur a penalty.

RATING: 3
Seasons is a good looking game with really good components, but it's something I'd rate as an investment game, i.e. it will definitely be best after many repeat plays. Unfortunately that is something I'm not willing to spend on this 2-player game. There are so many great, deep, and highly thematic 2-player games, and I don't think Seasons stand a chance against them.

While there's some Magic: The Gathering elements in the game, and you have to manage the change of the seasons, but in the end it just didn't feel tense and I wasn't invested in the gameplay.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I thought this game was going to be tough to learn with its odd looking dice and an intimidating stack of cards with lots of text. Instead it was very manageable, especially to those with a Magic the Gathering background. I thought all actions after choosing dice were simultaneous, so turns moved quickly in my games. Any card timing issues were determined by player order. After finding out the rules state one player finishes their turn, and then the next one plays--hm, no. I'll stick with simultaneous actions and a fast game, thanks!

RATING: 6.5
I received this from Matt Lust in the 2012 Dork Den Secret Santa Exchange. Thanks Matt!

The initial card draft is enjoyable here... though you need to wait for a lot of the game to be over to reap the rewards (unlike 7 Wonders or Fairy Tale where you use your clevery selected card immediately).  The dice draft limiting your turn (and sometimes leaving you with nothing at all you can do on your turn) can be frustrating, but when the card combos are clicking and the game doesn't bog down with too many power cards doing too many little things this can be pretty fun.... but it turned out to be a bad combination of a bit too long and a bit too thinky with too much downtime and randomness for my group so it was traded away.

RATING: 8.9
Seasons showed up in the geek buzz top 20 of Spiel 2012. We didn’t seen it there, never heard of it, but when we noticed it in the list, we looked at it, and became interested. Didn’t think of it, until we read a review of this game on one of the last days of 2012. In that review, there was said, that we would like the game very much. As we were very busy at that moment, we didn’t think much about it after that. Then we saw it popping up in a lot of ‘top 10 of ’12’ video’s. It popped up again. Started to watch some reviews and it seemed like fun to me, but would it be fun enough to own a copy of our own? I wasn’t sure. Then I discovered that we could play this game with two online. Of course, I didn’t know how the game worked, so I downloaded and printed the English set of rules. Explained the game to M., and after creating two new accounts, we were ready to play. M. played on her brand new tablet. I played on the laptop. Just perfect to try the game ourselves.

First thing I noticed was the artwork. When I first saw it, it somehow reminded me to Disney’s Alice in Wonderland. I don’t know why, except it just did. After taking a closer look, I thought Disney went mad! I love the artwork and the used colors. There fresh and bright, while the pictures on the cards sometimes look evil / dark. Just love it.

We liked the game, and while playing we said to each other that a digital copy of a boardgame doesn’t beat the feeling you have, when you’re rolling the dice. Holding the cards, and thinking of your next step, while you look your opponent in the eyes and your smelling the paper and wood. Bottomline to all of this. We just placed it on a shopping list, which is waiting to be filled with a copy of Bora Bora, which should be in stores any moment now.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
When I first started looking into this game, I had high hopes for it.  Then, I heard that it was on the lighter side of complexity, so my hopes waned.  The artwork looked so great, and I continued to find myself drawn to the components and reviews.  Finally, a guy in my gaming group brought it, and we played a three-player game.  We all loved it, and it was precisely what I wanted it to be.

This game fired 7 Wonders for most of us.  If 7 Wonders had this level of strategic drafting and mechanics, it would be so much better.  I mean, I still really enjoy 7 Wonders, but, after playing Seasons, I have to admit it fell down a rung on the proverbial ladder.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
